<tr>
<td class="noprint" colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><img alt="" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" width="33"/> <i><a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Bradford_City_A.F.C._season" title="2016–17 Bradford City A.F.C. season">Current season</a></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Bradford City Association Football Club</b> is a professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>, England. The team play in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One" title="Football League One">League One</a>, the third tier of <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football</a>.</p>
<p>The club was founded in 1903 and immediately elected into the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Football League Second Division</a>. Promotion to the top tier followed in 1908 and the club won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1911_FA_Cup_Final" title="1911 FA Cup Final">1911</a>, its only major honour. After relegation in 1922 from <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Division One</a>, the club spent 77 years outside the top flight until promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> in 1999. Relegation followed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000-01_Premier_League" title="2000-01 Premier League">2000–01</a> and since then a series of financial crises have pushed the club to the brink of closure and resulted in two more relegations to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" title="Football League Two">League Two</a>. In the 2012–13 season, they became the first team from the fourth tier of English football to reach the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup Final</a>, losing 5–0 to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swansea_City" title="Swansea City">Swansea City</a>. In the same season, they returned to Wembley for the playoff final and won promotion to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One" title="Football League One">League One</a> with a 3–0 win over Northampton Town.</p>
<p>The club's colours are claret and amber and they play home games at <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a>. The ground was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_stadium_fire" title="Bradford City stadium fire">Bradford City stadium fire</a> on 11 May 1985 which took the lives of 56 supporters.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stuart_McCall" title="Stuart McCall">Stuart McCall</a>, the current manager, was appointed in June 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bradford_City_A.F.C." title="History of Bradford City A.F.C.">History of Bradford City A.F.C.</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bradford_City_A.F.C._seasons" title="List of Bradford City A.F.C. seasons">List of Bradford City A.F.C. seasons</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bradford1911.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="458" data-file-width="717" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/45/Bradford1911.jpg/220px-Bradford1911.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/45/Bradford1911.jpg/330px-Bradford1911.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/45/Bradford1911.jpg/440px-Bradford1911.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bradford1911.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bradford City team which won the <a href="/wiki/1911_FA_Cup_Final" title="1911 FA Cup Final">1911 FA Cup</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bradford City were formed in 1903 as a result of a series of meetings called by James Whyte, a sub-editor of the <i>Bradford Observer</i>, with <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">Football Association</a> representatives and officials at <a href="/wiki/Manningham_F.C." title="Manningham F.C.">Manningham F.C.</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Football_League" title="The Football League">The Football League</a> saw the invitation as a chance to promote association football in the rugby league-dominated county of the <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding of Yorkshire</a>. It duly elected the new club into <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Division Two</a> of the league, in place of <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Rovers_F.C." title="Doncaster Rovers F.C.">Doncaster Rovers</a>. Four days later, at the 23rd annual meeting of Manningham FC, the committee decided to change code from rugby league to association football. Bradford City Association Football Club were formed without having played a game, taking over Manningham's colours of claret and amber, and their <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a> ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Campbell_(football_manager)" title="Robert Campbell (football manager)">Robert Campbell</a> was appointed the club's first manager and with the help of the new committee, he assembled a playing squad at the cost of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>917 10<a href="/wiki/Shilling" title="Shilling">s</a> 0<a href="/wiki/Penny" title="Penny">d</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f14_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-f14-5">[5]</a></sup> City's first game was a 2–0 defeat at <a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Town_F.C." title="Grimsby Town F.C.">Grimsby Town</a> on 1 September 1903,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> six days before their first home game attracted 11,000 fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f54_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-f54-7">[7]</a></sup> The club finished 10th in their first season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f14_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-f14-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_O%27Rourke" title="Peter O'Rourke">Peter O'Rourke</a> took over as manager in November 1905, and he led City to the Division Two title in <a href="/wiki/1907%E2%80%9308_in_English_football" title="1907–08 in English football">1907–08</a> and with it <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Division One</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orourke_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-orourke-8">[8]</a></sup> Having narrowly avoided relegation in their first season in the top flight, City recorded their highest finish of 5th in <a href="/wiki/1910%E2%80%9311_in_English_football" title="1910–11 in English football">1910–11</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The same season they won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>, when a goal from captain <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Speirs" title="Jimmy Speirs">Jimmy Speirs</a> won the <a href="/wiki/1911_FA_Cup_Final" title="1911 FA Cup Final">final</a> replay against <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> City's defence of the cup, which included the first <a href="/wiki/Bradford_derby" title="Bradford derby">Bradford derby</a> against <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Park_Avenue_A.F.C." title="Bradford Park Avenue A.F.C.">Bradford Park Avenue</a>, was stopped by <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a> after a run of 12 consecutive clean sheets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>City remained in the top flight in the period up to the First World War and for three seasons afterwards, but were relegated in <a href="/wiki/1921%E2%80%9322_in_English_football" title="1921–22 in English football">1921–22</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f21_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-f21-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Back in Division Two, attendances dropped and City struggled for form,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> with five consecutive finishes in the bottom half of the table. They suffered a second relegation to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division_North" title="Football League Third Division North">Division Three (North)</a> in <a href="/wiki/1926%E2%80%9327_in_English_football" title="1926–27 in English football">1926–27</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f21_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-f21-13">[13]</a></sup> Two seasons later, O'Rourke, who had initially retired in 1921 following the death of his son, returned and guided City to promotion with a record haul of 128 goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orourke_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-orourke-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> O'Rourke left for a second time after one more season, and although City spent a total of eight seasons back in Division Two, they rarely looked like earning promotion back to the top flight. Instead in <a href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%9337_in_English_football" title="1936–37 in English football">1936–37</a>, the club were relegated back to Division Three (North).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> City won their third piece of silverware two seasons later, when they lifted the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division_North_Cup" title="Football League Third Division North Cup">Third Division North Challenge Cup</a>, but they were unable to defend the trophy because competitive football was suspended for the Second World War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the war, City went through two managers in the first two seasons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and were consistently in the bottom half of the Division Three (North) table until <a href="/wiki/1955%E2%80%9356_in_English_football" title="1955–56 in English football">1955–56</a>. After three successive top half finishes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> City were placed in the new <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Division Three</a> in <a href="/wiki/1958%E2%80%9359_in_English_football" title="1958–59 in English football">1958–59</a>. Bradford spent just three seasons in Division Three, but during their relegation season in <a href="/wiki/1960%E2%80%9361_in_English_football" title="1960–61 in English football">1960–61</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f24_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-f24-21">[21]</a></sup> they upset Division One side Manchester United in the inaugural season of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> With 34 goals from <a href="/wiki/David_Layne" title="David Layne">David Layne</a>, City nearly earned an instant promotion the following season <a href="/wiki/1961%E2%80%9362_in_English_football" title="1961–62 in English football">1961–62</a>, but it did also include a record 9–1 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Colchester_United_F.C." title="Colchester United F.C.">Colchester United</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f24_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-f24-21">[21]</a></sup> Layne left for <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and without him City finished second from bottom of the league and had to apply for re-election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f24_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-f24-21">[21]</a></sup> Bradford City just failed to win promotion in <a href="/wiki/1963%E2%80%9364_in_English_football" title="1963–64 in English football">1963–64</a>, winning more games than any other team in the division that season, twenty five, with <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Green_(footballer)" title="Rodney Green (footballer)">Rodney Green</a> top scoring with 29 league goals. There followed three difficult seasons during which time manager <a href="/wiki/Grenville_Hair" title="Grenville Hair">Grenville Hair</a> died following a heart attack in training, City returned to Division Three getting promoted in <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_in_English_football" title="1968–69 in English football">1968–69</a>. City's stay in Division Three lasted just three years, when they finished bottom in <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_in_English_football" title="1971–72 in English football">1971–72</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Promotion via fourth spot was won again in <a href="/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_in_English_football" title="1976–77 in English football">1976–77</a> but it was instantly followed by a relegation season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f27_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-f27-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="380" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG/170px-Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG/255px-Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG/340px-Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade_Memorial.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A memorial, erected on the club's new main stand at <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a>, to the victims of the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_stadium_fire" title="Bradford City stadium fire">fire</a> in 1985</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>City failed to win promotion for three successive seasons, until the board appointed former <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre_back" title="Centre back">centre back</a> <a href="/wiki/Roy_McFarland" title="Roy McFarland">Roy McFarland</a> as manager in May 1981. McFarland won promotion in his first season, but was poached by his former club <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a> just six months later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f27_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-f27-25">[25]</a></sup> City won compensation from Derby and installed another England international <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Cherry" title="Trevor Cherry">Trevor Cherry</a> as McFarland's replacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Cherry, with former teammate <a href="/wiki/Terry_Yorath" title="Terry Yorath">Terry Yorath</a> as his assistant manager, failed to win for two months, but eventually the pair guided City to safety from relegation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> During the summer, however, the club chairman Bob Martin had to call in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Official_receiver" title="Official receiver">official receivers</a>. The club was saved by former chairman <a href="/wiki/Stafford_Heginbotham" title="Stafford Heginbotham">Stafford Heginbotham</a> and former board member Jack Tordoff, but to ensure the club could start the new season, prize asset, striker <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Campbell_(Northern_Irish_footballer)" title="Bobby Campbell (Northern Irish footballer)">Bobby Campbell</a> was sold to Derby. City struggled but so did Campbell, and when he returned, the club went on a record run of ten successive victories. Although they missed out on promotion, City won the league the following season <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_in_English_football" title="1984–85 in English football">1984–85</a>, to return to the second tier of The Football League. However, City's triumph was overshadowed by the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_stadium_fire" title="Bradford City stadium fire">fire disaster</a>, which killed 56 people when Valley Parade caught fire in the final game of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>City played games away from Valley Parade for 19 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> But just ten days after the new £2.6 million ground was opened, Cherry was sacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> His replacement, <a href="/wiki/Terry_Dolan_(footballer)" title="Terry Dolan (footballer)">Terry Dolan</a> steered City away from possible relegation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> before he mounted a promotion challenge the following season. City went top of the table in September 1987, but fell away during Christmas and missed out on promotion on the final day of the season. Instead they entered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship_play-offs" title="Football League Championship play-offs">play-offs</a>, but were defeated in the semi-finals by <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Two years later City were relegated back to Division Three. For three seasons, City finished mid-table in the third tier, which was renamed Division Two following the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="800" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg/220px-Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg/330px-Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg/440px-Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade_1990s.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bradford City against <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> at <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a> during the early 1990s</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January 1994, <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Richmond" title="Geoffrey Richmond">Geoffrey Richmond</a> came from <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_F.C." title="Scarborough F.C.">Scarborough</a> to take over as chairman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m165_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-m165-33">[33]</a></sup> and promised to guide City to the Premier League within five years. He cleared the debts and after four months sacked manager <a href="/wiki/Frank_Stapleton" title="Frank Stapleton">Frank Stapleton</a> to appoint his own manager, <a href="/wiki/Lennie_Lawrence" title="Lennie Lawrence">Lennie Lawrence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m165_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-m165-33">[33]</a></sup> Lawrence left after little more than a year to join <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a> but his successor, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Kamara" title="Chris Kamara">Chris Kamara</a> took City to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One_play-offs" title="Football League One play-offs">play-offs</a> and their first game at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>. They defeated <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a> 2–0 in the <a href="/wiki/1996_Football_League_Second_Division_play-off_Final" title="1996 Football League Second Division play-off Final">final</a> to earn promotion to Division One.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m165_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-m165-33">[33]</a></sup> City avoided relegation the following season by winning their last two league games 1–0 against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlton_Athletic" title="Charlton Athletic">Charlton</a> and then beating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers" title="Queens Park Rangers">Queens Park Rangers</a> 3–0 on the final day of the season, but Kamara was sacked in January 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Jewell" title="Paul Jewell">Paul Jewell</a> took over, initially on a temporary basis, before he was given a permanent contract. He bought the club's first £1 million signings and guided the club to the Premier League—the first time they had been in the top flight for 77 years—with a second-place finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The following season, Jewell continued to defy the critics, who labelled his team <i><a href="/wiki/Dad%27s_Army" title="Dad's Army">Dad's Army</a></i>, by avoiding relegation again on the last day with a 1–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, with a goal from <a href="/wiki/David_Wetherall" title="David Wetherall">David Wetherall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, Jewell left shortly afterwards. His assistant <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hutchings" title="Chris Hutchings">Chris Hutchings</a> was promoted to the manager's position,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and despite a series of new expensive signings,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> he was sacked by November 2000, with City second from bottom of the league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jefferies_(footballer)" title="Jim Jefferies (footballer)">Jim Jefferies</a> took over but could not save the club from relegation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> At the end of the first season back in Division One, City were placed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administration_(insolvency)" title="Administration (insolvency)">administration</a> with debts of nearly £13 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Two years later, the club suffered a second spell in administration and a second relegation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Two top-half finishes followed, but the club were relegated for a third time in seven seasons in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_in_English_football" title="2006–07 in English football">2006–07</a> meaning the following season would be their first in the bottom tier for 26 seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007_relegation_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-2007_relegation-47">[47]</a></sup> Former player <a href="/wiki/Stuart_McCall" title="Stuart McCall">Stuart McCall</a> was appointed the new manager,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and although he said anything less than promotion would be a failure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> he later changed his mind after a poor start and finally led the team to a 10th-place finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> McCall eventually left Bradford City on 8 February 2010 following a board meeting after a run of poor results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2011 the club became linked with American amateur side <a href="/wiki/SC_United_Bantams" title="SC United Bantams">SC United Bantams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2013, City became the first club from the fourth tier of English football since <a href="/wiki/Rochdale_A.F.C." title="Rochdale A.F.C.">Rochdale</a> in <a href="/wiki/1961%E2%80%9362_Football_League_Cup" title="1961–62 Football League Cup">1962</a> to reach the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> final, and the first fourth tier club ever to reach a major Wembley Cup Final. They defeated three <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> sides en route to the final – <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> 4–2 on penalties in the fourth round, <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> 3–2 on penalties in the quarter-finals and <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> 4–3 on aggregate over the two legs of the semi-final. They met Premier League side <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2013 Football League Cup Final">final</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a>, but lost 0–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The run to the final is thought to be worth at least £1.3 million to the club, with the club's joint chairman Mark Lawn stating that the final itself could be worth an additional £1 million, taking the clubs total earnings to £2.3 million during their <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Football_League_Cup" title="2012–13 Football League Cup">2012–13 Football League Cup</a> campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> On 18 May 2013, the club returned to <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a> where they defeated <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Town_F.C." title="Northampton Town F.C.">Northampton Town F.C.</a> 3–0 in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/League_Two" title="League Two">League Two</a> Playoff Final to secure a place in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One" title="Football League One">League One</a> for 2013–14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 January 2015, Bradford City caused an upset by beating Premiership-leaders <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> 4–2 away in the FA Cup. The victory sent Bradford through to the 5th round for the first time in eighteen years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> They beat <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>, another Premier League club, 2–0 at home in the next round on 15 February 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In the Quarter Finals, The Bantams faced <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading F.C.</a>, also a Premier League club, at home, a game that ended in a goalless draw. The replay was played on 16 March 2015 at the Madejski Stadium, where Reading won 3–0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and knocked the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One" title="Football League One">third-tier division</a> club out of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours_and_club_crest">Colours and club crest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colours and club crest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bradford City is the only professional football club in England to wear claret and amber. The club colours were inherited from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manningham_FC" title="Manningham FC">Manningham FC</a>, when the club converted to football upon Bradford City's foundation in 1903. However, whereas Manningham played in hoops, the new football club adopted claret and amber stripes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Manningham RFC adopted the colours in 1884 before the move to Valley Parade in 1886. Having originally worn black shirts with white shorts, the club's first game in claret and amber was against Hull on 20 September 1884, at Carlisle Road.</p>
<p>The reason Manningham chose claret and amber is not documented but it was the same colours of <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Regiment" title="West Yorkshire Regiment">The Prince of Wales's Own West Yorkshire Regiment</a>, which was based at Belle Vue Barracks on nearby Manningham Lane. Both Manningham, from 1886, and Bradford City, from 1903 to 1908, used the barracks as changing and club rooms.</p>
<p>Bradford City has worn claret and amber, with either white or black, since it was founded. Since the fire in 1985, the club has used black on the kit as a memorial to the 56 supporters who died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-All_white_change_strip_for_next_season_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-All_white_change_strip_for_next_season-62">[62]</a></sup> The club's away shirt has traditionally been white and to a lesser extent also blue, but there has been a profusion of other colours and designs particularly in more recent years. The away kit for the 2008–09 season was all white.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-All_white_change_strip_for_next_season_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-All_white_change_strip_for_next_season-62">[62]</a></sup> For the new 2009–10 season, the away kit will be all black with a thin claret and amber stripe down the centre-left.</p>
<p>City scarves have also sold in large numbers in recent years to fans of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Potter</a></i>, because the colours are the same as Harry's house scarf at <a href="/wiki/Hogwarts" title="Hogwarts">Hogwarts School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of other clubs across the world wear claret and amber. They include Scottish club <a href="/wiki/Motherwell_F.C." title="Motherwell F.C.">Motherwell</a>, who originally wore blue and white until they wore claret and amber for the first time on 23 August 1913, against Celtic. It is erroneously believed that Motherwell chose the claret and amber colours because they were the racing colours of Lord Hamilton; it is more likely that Motherwell were influenced by Bradford City's English FA cup win in 1911.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club's crest combines a series of logos from over the years. In 1974, City adopted a contemporary style crest incorporating the club's initials, with a B-C logo. At the time, the new logo maintained the previous nickname of the Paraders. By December 1981, the club relaunched the Bantams as the official identity with a bantam on the new crest. The crest maintains the club colours and also includes the words The Bantams.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname">Nickname</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Nickname">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bradford City have had a number of nicknames during the history. In their early years, they were referred to as the Robins or Wasps, taking over the nickname of Manningham FC, as a result of Manningham's claret and amber hoops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f14_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-f14-5">[5]</a></sup> Other nicknames have been the Citizens or Paraders, but the club is better known as the Bantams.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_stadium_fire" title="Bradford City stadium fire">Bradford City stadium fire</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a> was the site of a <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">quarry</a> on the hillside below <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham, Bradford</a>, owned by Midland Railway Company, in 1886, when Manningham RFC bought one-third of the land and leased the remainder, because they had been forced to find a new home. They spent <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>1,400 erecting a ground with a capacity of 20,000, club facilities and levelling the land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f53_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-f53-65">[65]</a></sup> When Bradford City were formed in 1903, they took over the ground Valley Parade, which was also at this time the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_Artillery" title="West Riding Artillery">The 2nd West Riding Brigade Royal Field Artillery (Territorial Force)</a>, playing their first home game on 5 September 1903 against <a href="/wiki/Gainsborough_Trinity_F.C." title="Gainsborough Trinity F.C.">Gainsborough Trinity</a>, drawing a crowd of 11,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f54_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-f54-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Five years later, the club won promotion to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Division One</a>, and so commissioned football architect <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Leitch" title="Archibald Leitch">Archibald Leitch</a> to redevelop the ground. The capacity was increased to 40,000 by December 1908 with a 5,300-seater main stand, a <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(stadium)" title="Terrace (stadium)">terraced</a> paddock in front, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spion_Kop_(stadia)" title="Spion Kop (stadia)">Spion Kop</a>, and an 8,000-capacity Midland Road stand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Its first game against <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a> on Christmas Day attracted a crowd of 36,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d1_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-d1-68">[68]</a></sup> On 11 March 1911, Valley Parade attracted its highest attendance 39,146, for an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> game between Bradford City and <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a> during Bradford's <a href="/wiki/1911_FA_Cup_Final" title="1911 FA Cup Final">FA Cup winning run</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Until 1952, by which time Bradford City had bought the remaining two-thirds of the ground to own it outright,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f56_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-f56-70">[70]</a></sup> the ground remained virtually unchanged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d1_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-d1-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> However, twice during the next decade, the club's Midland Road stand had to be demolished. Club officials first closed part of the stand in 1952, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Burnden_Park_disaster" title="Burnden Park disaster">Burnden Park disaster</a> six years earlier. Its frame was sold to <a href="/wiki/Berwick_Rangers_F.C." title="Berwick Rangers F.C.">Berwick Rangers</a> and a replacement stand built in 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f56_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-f56-70">[70]</a></sup> Six years later, the new stand was itself demolished, and Valley Parade remained a three-sided ground until 1966, when the pitch was moved, and a new stand built.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="528" data-file-width="704" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG/220px-Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG/330px-Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG/440px-Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade_Away_Stand.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bradford End of <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a>, which was the first to be redeveloped after the ground reopened in 1986</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 11 May 1985, Valley Parade was the scene of a <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_stadium_fire" title="Bradford City stadium fire">fatal fire</a>, during which 56 supporters were killed and at least 265 were injured. The game was the final match of the <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_in_English_football" title="1984–85 in English football">1984–85</a> season, before which City were presented with the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Division Three</a> championship trophy. The fire destroyed the main stand in just nine minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-f53_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-f53-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The club played its home games at <a href="/wiki/Odsal_Stadium" title="Odsal Stadium">Odsal Stadium</a>, a rugby league ground in Bradford, <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a>, Leeds, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leeds_Road,_Huddersfield" title="Leeds Road, Huddersfield">Leeds Road</a>, the former home of Huddersfield Town, until December 1986, while Valley Parade was redeveloped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The club spent £2.6 million building a new main stand and improving the Kop, and reopened the new ground on 14 December 1986 for an exhibition match against an England international XI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1991, the Bradford end of the ground was the next to be redeveloped, and was converted into a two-tier stand with a scoreboard. In 1996, following City's promotion to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Division_One" title="Football League Division One">Division One</a>, club chairman <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Richmond" title="Geoffrey Richmond">Geoffrey Richmond</a> announced the construction of a 4,500 seater stand on the Midland Road side. Ahead of promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premiership</a> in 1999, Richmond spent another £6.5 million to convert the Kop into a two-tier 7,500-seat capacity stand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vp_history_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-vp_history-76">[76]</a></sup> A corner stand between the Kop and main stand was opened in December 2000, taking the capacity to 20,000 for the first time since 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The following summer, the main stand was also converted into a two-tier stand, taking the capacity to 25,136. Further projects were planned until the club went into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administration_(insolvency)" title="Administration (insolvency)">administration</a> in May 2002 so none have taken place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vp_history_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-vp_history-76">[76]</a></sup> The following year, Valley Parade was sold to Gibb's pension fund for £5 million, with the club's offices, the shop and car park sold to London-based Development Securities for £2.5 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> but these (club offices, shop and car park) were bought back by the club's joint chairmen in the summer of 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The club's annual rent and maintenance costs to Gibb's pension fund is £1.2m, and so as of February 2009, the club is considering a return to Odsal. The club and Bradford Bulls would share the new £50m complex, which would also feature <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, cycling and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_and_field_athletics" title="Track and field athletics">athletics</a> facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Valley Parade has had several other names under sponsorship naming deals and as of July 2016 is called the Northern Commercials Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The club spearheaded an initiative in 2007 to slash the price of watching professional football for the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_in_English_football" title="2007–08 in English football">2007–08</a> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> As a result, season tickets to watch Bradford City were the cheapest in England at £138, the equivalent of £6 per match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> When the offer finished at 7 pm on Tuesday, 31 July 2007, the club confirmed the amount of season tickets sold was 12,019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The scheme enabled the club to top the average league attendances for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" title="Football League Two">Football League Two</a> during the 2007–08 season, attracting more than three times more than any other club. The club won the Perform Best Fan Marketing campaign category in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Football_League_Awards" title="The Football League Awards">The Football League Awards</a> for the scheme and earned them an invitation to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament" title="Houses of Parliament">Houses of Parliament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The club aimed to attract 20,000 fans for the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_in_English_football" title="2008–09 in English football">2008–09</a> by offering a free season ticket to anyone buying a season ticket as long as 9,000 adults sign up, but they fell 704 short of the target.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Joint-chairman Mark Lawn announced in November 2008 that season tickets in the Bradford End for the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_in_English_football" title="2009–10 in English football">2009–10</a> season would be available for just £99 and £138 for the rest of the ground if bought in December 2008.</p>
<p>Season tickets for the 2013–14 season are available until 31 July 2013. Adults prices are £199, senior citizen and student tickets priced at £149 and juniors £99. For the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_in_English_football" title="2015–16 in English football">2015–16</a> season, the club announced its latest season ticket scheme aimed at continuing to make football affordable for fans. Season ticket prices were set at £149 for adults, senior citizens and students, while admission for under-11s was free when purchased with an adult ticket. An initial campaign target of 15,000 was set with a deadline for the reduced tickets of 31 July 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On 6 July, the club announced a record breaking 18,000 tickets had been sold following a successful campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The campaign was repeated for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2016-17_Bradford_City_A.F.C._season" title="2016-17 Bradford City A.F.C. season">2016–17 season</a>, where the club sold in excess of 17,000 tickets.</p>
<p>Bradford City have one official <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascot</a>, Billy Bantam.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry">Rivalry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rivalry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bradford_derby" title="Bradford derby">Bradford derby</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_derby" title="West Yorkshire derby">West Yorkshire derby</a></div>
<p>Bradford City have participated in the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_derby" title="Bradford derby">Bradford derby</a> with city rivals <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Park_Avenue_A.F.C." title="Bradford Park Avenue A.F.C.">Park Avenue</a>. The <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_derby" title="West Yorkshire derby">West Yorkshire derby</a> is held between City and local rivals <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_F.C." title="Huddersfield Town F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> A "friendly" rivalry also existed with now-defunct club <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Town_A.F.C." title="Halifax Town A.F.C.">Halifax Town</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_football">European football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: European football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bradford City competed in the Intertoto Cup of 2000 alongside <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aston_Villa" title="Aston Villa">Aston Villa</a> as fellow English sides in the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_players">Former players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Former players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bradford_City_A.F.C._players" title="List of Bradford City A.F.C. players">List of Bradford City A.F.C. players</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Bradford_City_A.F.C._players_with_fewer_than_50_league_appearances" title="List of Bradford City A.F.C. players with fewer than 50 league appearances">List of Bradford City A.F.C. players with fewer than 50 league appearances</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Bradford_City_A.F.C._players" title="Category:Bradford City A.F.C. players">Category:Bradford City A.F.C. players</a></div>
<p>In 2007 former <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradford_Telegraph_and_Argus" title="Bradford Telegraph and Argus">Telegraph &amp; Argus</a></i> sports journalist David Markham released the book <i>The Legends of Bradford City</i>, initially written to mark the club's centenary in 2003. It featured biographies of 100 players and staff members from the history of the club. The players were:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_City_A.F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1327" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg/220px-Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg/330px-Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg/440px-Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bradford_City_FC_League_Performance.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A graph showing Bradford City's league history</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Record league victory: <b>11–1</b> v <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>, Division Three (North), 25 August 1928</li>
<li>Record FA Cup victory: <b>11–3</b> v Walker Celtic, First Round Replay, 1 December 1937</li>
<li>Record League Cup victory: <b>7–2</b> v <a href="/wiki/Darlington_F.C." title="Darlington F.C.">Darlington</a>, Second Round Second Leg, 25 September 2000</li>
<li>Record league defeat: <b>0–8</b> v <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>, Division Two, 7 May 1927 / <b>1–9</b> v <a href="/wiki/Colchester_United_F.C." title="Colchester United F.C.">Colchester United</a>, Division Four, 30 December 1961</li>
<li>Record FA Cup defeat: <b>1–6</b> v <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, Third Round, 7 March 1963 / <b>0–5</b> v <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, Fifth Round Replay, 3 February 1960 / <b>0–5</b> v <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>, Third Round, 7 January 1970</li>
<li>Record home attendance: <b>39,146</b> v <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, FA Cup Fourth Round, 11 March 1911</li>
<li>Record gate receipts: <b>£300,000</b> v <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal F.C.</a>, Capital One Cup Quarter Final, 11 December 2012</li>
<li>Longest unbeaten run : <b>21</b> 1968 to 1969</li>
<li>Longest run of wins: <b>10</b> 1983 to 1984</li>
<li>Most appearances : <b>574</b> <a href="/wiki/Ces_Podd" title="Ces Podd">Ces Podd</a></li>
<li>Most league appearances: <b>502</b> – <a href="/wiki/Ces_Podd" title="Ces Podd">Ces Podd</a></li>
<li>Most goals scored : <b>143</b> – <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Campbell_(Northern_Irish_footballer)" title="Bobby Campbell (Northern Irish footballer)">Bobby Campbell</a></li>
<li>Most league goals: <b>121</b> – <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Campbell_(Northern_Irish_footballer)" title="Bobby Campbell (Northern Irish footballer)">Bobby Campbell</a></li>
<li>Most goals in a season: <b>36</b> – <a href="/wiki/David_Layne" title="David Layne">David Layne</a>, <a href="/wiki/1961%E2%80%9362_in_English_football" title="1961–62 in English football">1961–62</a></li>
<li>Most goals scored in a match: <b>7</b> – <a href="/wiki/Albert_Whitehurst" title="Albert Whitehurst">Albert Whitehurst</a> v <a href="/wiki/Tranmere_Rovers_F.C." title="Tranmere Rovers F.C.">Tranmere Rovers</a>, Division Three (North), 6 March 1929</li>
<li>Highest transfer fee paid: <b>£2.5 million</b> – <a href="/wiki/David_Hopkin" title="David Hopkin">David Hopkin</a>, from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leeds_United_A.F.C." title="Leeds United A.F.C.">Leeds United</a>, July 2000</li>
<li>Highest transfer fee received: <b>£2 million</b> – <a href="/wiki/Des_Hamilton" title="Des Hamilton">Des Hamilton</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, March 1997 / <a href="/wiki/Andy_O%27Brien_(footballer)" title="Andy O'Brien (footballer)">Andy O'Brien</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, March 2001</li>
<li>Most team league goals in a season: <b>128</b> – Division Three (North), <a href="/wiki/1928%E2%80%9329_in_English_football" title="1928–29 in English football">1928–29</a></li>
<li>Most points (three points for a win): <b>94</b> – Division Three, <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_in_English_football" title="1984–85 in English football">1984–85</a></li>
<li>Most points (two points for a win): <b>63</b> – Division Three (North), <a href="/wiki/1928%E2%80%9329_in_English_football" title="1928–29 in English football">1928–29</a></li>
</ul>
<p><i>All records from Bradford City F.C. official website</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
